D) They are opposites.

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq is synonymous with knowledge and belief in classical usage, but when applied to faith it requires additional conditions like choice and sincerity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have read that tasdiq (assent) is considered a kind of knowledge but is conditioned by choice and abandonment of denial. Reflect: In your faith, do you merely assent intellectually, or have you consciously chosen to submit? What keeps you from surrendering fully?
?
Ali's chain—'Faith is knowledge, knowledge is submission, submission is assent'—shows a progression. Which step do you find most challenging: truly knowing God, submitting to that knowledge, or allowing that submission to produce heartfelt assent? Why?
?
The author says faith requires 'acquisition, choice, and abandoning denial and arrogance.' Look honestly at your own life: is there an area where you are still in denial or arrogance, refusing to let your knowledge become submission? What will you do today to move from knowing about God to actively submitting to Him?

The Third Argument: Tasdiq is a Quality, Not an Act
The third argument that tasdiq is a quality (kayfiyya) of the soul, not an act

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third argument that tasdiq (assent) is a quality of the soul, not an act, and why this distinction matters for the nature of faith.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is a quality of the soul, not a momentary act.

This passage presents the third argument from the author to establish that tasdiq (assent) is a quality (kayfiyya) of the soul, not an act (fi'l). The author defines tasdiq as the heart's submission and acceptance, without any action or effect, and argues that it can be obtained with or without choice. This distinction is crucial for understanding faith: while faith must be chosen, its essence is a stable quality, not a fleeting act.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage aloud, then the English translation. Notice the author's confident tone and his use of logical argumentation.
Pay attention to the key terms: التصديق, الكيف, الفعل.
2
Identify the main claim
The author states that tasdiq is a quality of the soul. Find the sentence where he says 'we are certain that this is a quality.'
3
Understand how quality is obtained
The author explains that this quality can be obtained either by choice and means or without them. Consider why this flexibility is important.
This shows that tasdiq is not inherently tied to volition.
4
Analyze the rejection of the counterclaim
The author rejects the view that tasdiq is an act and argues that if it were, one could only be described as having faith while performing the act. Think about the problem this creates.
5
Reflect on the implication for faith
The author allows that for faith, acquisition by choice is required, but the nature of tasdiq itself is a quality. This reconciles the settled nature of faith with the requirement of free will.
This argument guards against reducing faith to a momentary act.

الثالث - أنا لا نفهم من نسبة الصدق إلى المتكلم بالقلب سوى إذعانه وقبوله وإدراكه لهذا المعنى . أعني كون المتكلم صادقاً من غير أن يتصور هناك فعل وتأثير من القلب. ونقطع بأن هذا كيفية للنفس قد تحصل بالكسب والاختيار ومباشرة الأسباب، وقد تحصل بدونها . فغاية الأمر أن يشترط فيما اعتبر الإيمان أن يكون تحصيله بالاختيار على ما هو قاعدة المأمور به . واما أن هذا فعل وتأثير من النفس لا كيفية لها وأن الاختيار معتبر في مفهوم التصديق اللغوي فممنوع ، بل معلوم الانتفاء قطعاً . ولو كان الإيمان والتصديق من مقولة الفعل دون الكيف لما صح الاتصاف به حقيقة إلا حال المباشرة والتحصيل كما لا يخفى على من يعرف معنى هذه المقولة .
Third: We do not understand from the attribution of truthfulness to the speaker by the heart anything other than its (the heart's) submission, acceptance, and perception of this meaning — that is, that the speaker is truthful, without there being imagined any action or effect from the heart. And we are certain that this is a quality (kayfiyya) of the soul, which may be obtained by acquisition, choice, and directly employing the means, and may be obtained without them. So the utmost that can be required in that which is considered as faith is that its acquisition be by choice, according to the rule of the commanded. As for the claim that this is an act and effect of the soul, not a quality, and that choice is a condition in the linguistic concept of assent (tasdiq), it is rejected; rather, it is known to be false categorically. And if faith and assent were from the category of act rather than quality, it would not be valid to be truly described by them except at the moment of performance and acquisition, as is not hidden from one who knows the meaning of these categories.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is a proof (the third argument) that tasdiq (assent) is a quality (kayfiyya) of the soul, not an act (fi'l). The author begins by defining what he means by assenting with the heart: it is simply the heart's submission, acceptance, and perception of the speaker's truthfulness, without imagining any act or effect from the heart. This is a quality. The author then asserts that this quality may be obtained either by choice and means (kash and ikhtiyar) or without them. For faith, acquisition by choice is required, but the nature of tasdiq itself is not dependent on volition. He rejects the alternative view that tasdiq is an act of the soul, arguing that if it were an act, one could only be described as having faith while performing the act, which is problematic. This guards against the misunderstanding that faith is a momentary act rather than a settled quality.

Correction: The author argues that tasdiq is a quality that can exist without choice, though faith must be acquired by choice. If it were an act, one could not be described as having faith except during the act itself.

Faith and Disbelief

The fourth argument: tasdiq is of the genus of knowledge and belief
The fourth argument equating tasdiq with ma'rifa and i'tiqad, citing scholarly usage and Ali's hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth argument that equates tasdiq (assent) with ma'rifa (knowledge) and i'tiqad (belief), including the qualification that tasdiq in faith is conditioned by free choice and absence of denial and arrogance.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is a type of knowledge, but in faith it requires free choice and avoidance of arrogance.

This lesson presents the fourth argument that tasdiq (assent) belongs to the genus of knowledge and belief. The author notes that many scholars use 'ma'rifa' and 'i'tiqad' interchangeably with 'tasdiq', and supports this with a famous statement from Ali (رضي الله عنه). However, he also specifies that in the context of faith, tasdiq is tied to conditions like being acquired by choice and being free from denial and arrogance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation. Notice how the author builds his argument: first an observation, then an inference, then evidence.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage opens with the observation that many great scholars use 'ma'rifa' or 'i'tiqad' in place of 'tasdiq'. This suggests that tasdiq is of the same genus as knowledge and belief.
The word 'كرويدن' is a transliteration of 'credence' (from Latin), indicating the concept of belief.
3
Note the condition for faith
Despite tasdiq being of the genus of knowledge, in the context of faith it is restricted by conditions: it must be acquired through free choice and must be free from denial and arrogance.
These conditions distinguish theological faith from mere assent.
4
Examine the hadith evidence
The author cites Ali's statement: 'Faith is knowledge, knowledge is submission, submission is assent.' This chain establishes that tasdiq is a form of knowledge (ma'rifa).
Trace the chain: iman → ma'rifa → taslim → tasdiq. Tasdiq is the final and core component.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع - أنه وقع في كلام كثير من عظماء الملة، وعلماء الأمة مكان لفظ التصديق لفظ المعرفة والاعتقاد فينبغي أن يحمل على العلم التصديق المعبر عنه بكرويدن، ويقطع بأن التصديق من جنس العلوم والاعتقادات، لكنه في الإيمان مشروط بقيود و خصوصيات كالتحصيل والاختيار، وترك الجحود والاستكبار. ويدل على ذلك ما ذكره أمير المؤمنين (علي كرم الله وجهه) أن الإيمان معرفة، والمعرفة تسليم، والتسليم تصديق
Fourth: It occurs in the speech of many great ones of the religion and scholars of the community that the term 'assent' (tasdiq) is replaced by the term 'knowledge' (ma'rifa) or 'belief' (i'tiqad). So it should be understood as the knowledge of assent, which is expressed as 'credence' (kruwidan?), and it is certain that assent is of the genus of knowledges and beliefs, but in faith it is conditioned by restrictions and specificities such as acquisition, choice, and abandonment of denial and arrogance. Evidence for this is what the Commander of the Faithful (Ali, may God honor his face) mentioned: 'Faith is knowledge, knowledge is submission, and submission is assent.'
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is the fourth argument that tasdiq is a type of knowledge (ma'rifa) or belief (i'tiqad). The author notes that many scholars use 'ma'rifa' and 'i'tiqad' in place of 'tasdiq'. He says that tasdiq should be understood as the 'knowledge of assent' (or 'credence'), and it is certain that tasdiq is of the genus of knowledges and beliefs. However, for faith, tasdiq is conditioned by specific restrictions like being acquired by choice and being free from denial and arrogance. He then cites the hadith of Ali (رضي الله عنه) that establishes a chain: faith is knowledge (ma'rifa), knowledge is submission (taslim), and submission is assent (tasdiq). This supports the claim that tasdiq is a kind of knowledge.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that tasdiq (assent) is not a kind of knowledge, but rather a separate category.
Correction: The passage explicitly equates tasdiq with ma'rifa and i'tiqad, and cites scholarly usage and a hadith to show that tasdiq belongs to the genus of knowledge and belief.

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq (assent) is a type of knowledge, but in the context of faith, it must be accompanied by free choice and freedom from denial and arrogance.

The Objection and Redefinition of Inner Speech
Objection and answer redefining inner speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the objection that tasdiq is inner speech is answered by redefining inner speech to include all psychological states.

Core Idea
Inner speech includes all mental content, so calling tasdiq inner speech doesn't make it non-knowledge.

This lesson addresses a key objection raised by Imams al-Haramayn and al-Razi: that tasdiq is a form of inner speech distinct from knowledge and will. The response redefines inner speech itself, expanding it to cover anything in the soul that can be expressed. This reframing shows that the objection does not automatically exclude tasdiq from being a type of knowledge or will.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the citation of the imams and the immediate response.
2
Understand the redefinition of inner speech
The answer redefines kalam al-nafs to include all psychological content that can be indicated by utterance, writing, or gesture. This is key.
3
Identify why this matters
Ask yourself: if inner speech includes knowledge and will, then calling tasdiq inner speech does not separate it from knowledge. The objection collapses.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : قد ذكر إمام الحرمين، والإمام الرازي وغيرهما أن التصديق من جنس كلام النفس، وكلام النفس غير العلم والإرادة .
قلنا : معناه أنه ليس بمتعين أن يكون علماً أو إرادة، بل كل ما يحصل في النفس من حيث يدل عليه بعبارة أو كتابة أو إشارة، فهو كلام النفس، سواء كان علماً، أو إرادة أو طلباً، أو إخباراً، أو استخباراً، أو غير ذلك. وليس كلام النفس نوعاً من المعاني مغايراً لما هو حاصل في النفس باتفاق الفرق، وإلا كان إنكاره إنكاراً للتصديق والطلب والإخبار، والاستخبار، وسائر ما يحصل في القلب وليس كذلك، بل إنكاره عائد إلى أن الكلام هو المسموع فقط دون هذه المعاني . فالقول بأن الإيمان كلام النفس لا يكفي في التقصي عن مطالبته أنه من أي نوع من أنواع الأغراض وأية مقولة من المقولات؟ ولا محیص سوى تسليم أنه من الكيفيات النفسية الحاصلة بالاختيار، الخالية عن الجحود والاستكبار وليت شعري أنه إذا لم يكن من جنس العلوم والاعتقادات، فما معنى تحصيله بالدليل أو التقليد؟ وهل يعقل بأن يكون ثمرة النظر والاستدلال غير العلم والاعتقاد، وكلام كثير من ذوي التحصيل القائلين بالتصديق يدل على أنهم لا يعنون بالمعرفة التي لا تكفي في الإيمان معرفة حقية ما جاء به النبي . قال أبو المعين النسفي في تبصرة الأدلة : لا يلزم من انعدام العلم انعدام التصديق. فإنا آمنا بالملائكة والكتب والرسل، ولا نعرفهم بأعيانهم . والمعاندون يعرفون ولا يصدقون ، كما قال الله تعالى : الذين آتيناهم الكتاب
If it is said: The Imam al-Haramayn, Imam al-Razi, and others have mentioned that assent (tasdiq) is of the genus of inner speech (kalam al-nafs), and inner speech is other than knowledge and will.
We say: Its meaning is that it is not specified to be knowledge or will; rather, everything that occurs in the soul in terms of being indicated by an utterance, writing, or gesture is inner speech, whether it is knowledge, will, a request, a statement, a question, or something else. And inner speech is not a type of meanings distinct from what occurs in the soul, by agreement of the schools; otherwise, its denial would be a denial of assent, request, statement, question, and all that occurs in the heart. But it is not like that; rather, its denial refers to the fact that speech is only what is heard, without these meanings. So the statement that faith is inner speech is not sufficient to inquire about its demand: which type of purposes and which category of categories does it belong to? There is no escape except to admit that it is from the psychological qualities (al-kayfiyyat al-nafsiyya) that occur by choice, free from denial and arrogance. I wonder, if it is not of the genus of knowledges and beliefs, what is the meaning of its acquisition by proof or blind following? Is it conceivable that the fruit of speculation and inference is other than knowledge and belief? And the speech of many scholars who say assent indicates that they do not mean by knowledge that which is insufficient for faith: the genuine knowledge of what the Prophet brought. Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi said in Tabṣirat al-Adilla: 'The absence of knowledge does not entail the absence of assent. For we believe in the angels, books, and messengers, but we do not know them in their persons. And the obstinate people know (them) but do not assent, as God Almighty said: Those to whom We gave the Book...'
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer followed by further argument. The objection cites Imams al-Haramayn and al-Razi that tasdiq is of the genus of inner speech (kalam al-nafs), distinct from knowledge and will. The answer redefines inner speech broadly: it includes anything in the soul expressed by utterance, writing, or gesture, so knowledge, will, requests, etc., are all inner speech. The author argues that inner speech is not a distinct type of meaning; otherwise, denying it would mean denying many things like tasdiq, requests, etc. The objection's denial actually means they only consider audible speech as speech. Therefore, calling faith 'inner speech' does not specify which category it belongs to; it must be admitted as a psychological quality (kayfiyya nafsiyya) acquired by choice, free from denial and arrogance. The author then questions: if tasdiq is not from the genus of knowledge and belief, how can it be acquired by proof or taqlid? The fruit of speculation is knowledge and belief. He cites al-Nasafi to show that knowledge and tasdiq are separable: one can believe without detailed knowledge (angels, books), and obstinate people know but do not believe (Quranic verse). This reinforces that tasdiq is a quality distinct from detailed knowledge.

Key Terms
كلام النفس
التصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That tasdiq as inner speech means it is separate from knowledge and will and thus cannot be a psychological quality.
Correction: The author shows that inner speech is a broad category including knowledge and will, so tasdiq being inner speech does not preclude it from being a quality.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what is included in inner speech (kalam al-nafs)?
A) Only knowledge and will
B) All psychological content that can be expressed by utterance, writing, or gesture
C) Only requests and statements
D) Only audible speech

Key Takeaway
Inner speech is a comprehensive category that includes all mental content expressible by signs, not a separate type of meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Do you treat them as seriously as the words you speak aloud, knowing that Allah hears and knows them all? What would change in your daily life if you recognized that your inner speech is real, accountable speech?
?
This lesson argues that inner speech includes not just knowledge and will, but also your deepest assumptions and acts of assent. Is the tasdiq in your heart—the faith you claim—actually present as a true inner conviction, or is it just a label? When was the last time you examined whether your inner speech aligns with what you profess with your tongue?

Tasdiq as a Psychological Quality and the Separability of Knowledge and Assent
Conclusion that tasdiq is a psychological quality with supporting argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why tasdiq must be a psychological quality distinct from knowledge, and how one can have assent without detailed knowledge.

Core Idea
Tasdiq is a volitional psychological quality, not reducible to knowledge or belief.

After redefining inner speech, the author draws the conclusion: calling faith 'inner speech' is insufficient to specify its category. The only tenable position is that it is a psychological quality (kayfiyya nafsiyya) acquired by choice, free from denial and arrogance. This lesson also explores a supporting argument from Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi, who notes that one can believe in angels without knowing them individually, and obstinate people know but do not assent—proving that knowledge and tasdiq are separable.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage from 'فالقول' to the end
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the question about which category tasdiq belongs to.
2
Identify the conclusion about tasdiq
The author argues that tasdiq must be a psychological quality (kayfiyya nafsiyya) that occurs by choice, free from denial and arrogance.
3
Understand al-Nasafi's argument
Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi distinguishes between knowledge and assent: we believe in angels without detailed knowledge, and obstinate people know but do not believe. This shows tasdiq is not simply knowledge.

C) The absence of inner speech
D) The absence of will

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq is a volitional psychological quality distinct from knowledge, as shown by the possibility of assent without detailed knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The obstinate people know the truth but do not assent. Is there any truth in your life—about yourself, your relationship with Allah, or your actions—that you know but refuse to personally submit to? What would it take for you to move from knowledge to tasdiq today?
?
You believe in angels and the unseen without detailed knowledge. Is your heart truly at peace with that mystery, or do you secretly demand full comprehension before you submit? Where are you holding back trust?
?
Tasdiq is a quality of the soul acquired by choice. Right now, what is your soul choosing—denial and arrogance or humble assent? Make one concrete decision today that proves your tasdiq is not just information in your mind but a settled conviction of your heart.

Tasdiq and Knowledge: Two Separate Things
Al-Nasafi argues for the disjunction of tasdiq and knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that tasdiq (affirmation of the heart) can exist independently of knowledge (ilm), and why faith is not simply knowledge.

Core Idea
Tasdiq and knowledge can dissociate; faith is not reducible to knowledge.

Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi presents a critical argument in the science of kalam: the absence of knowledge does not entail the absence of tasdiq. Using examples of believers and obstinate unbelievers, he shows that tasdiq and knowledge are separable. This leads to the refutation of Jahm ibn Safwan's view that faith is identical to knowledge. Let's explore his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the two examples used: believers and obstinate ones.
2
Identify the two examples
Find the example of believers (we believe in angels etc. without knowing them) and the example of obstinate ones (they know but don't tasdiq). How does each support the disjunction?
The Quranic citation strengthens the second example.
3
Understand the conclusion
Al-Nasafi concludes that tasdiq and knowledge can be separate. Therefore, faith is not simply knowledge, contra Jahm ibn Safwan.
This has implications for defining faith in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو المعين النسفي في تبصرة الأدلة : لا يلزم من انعدام العلم انعدام التصديق. فإنا آمنا بالملائكة والكتب والرسل، ولا نعرفهم بأعيانهم . والمعاندون يعرفون ولا يصدقون ، كما قال الله تعالى : الذين آتيناهم الكتاب (۲) فدل على انفكاك التصديق عن العلم والعلم عن التصديق . ولهذا لم يجعل الإيمان معرفة على ما ذهب إليه جهم بن صفوان . الخامس - أن ما ذكر من اعتبار الاختيار في نفس التصديق اللغوي، وكون الحاصل بلا كسب واختيار ليس بإيمان يدل على أن تصديق الملائكة بما ألقى عليهم، والأنبياء بما أوحي إليهم، والمصدقين بما سمعوا من النبي (عليه السلام كله مكتسب بالاختيار. وأن من حصل له هذا المعنى بلا كسب كمن شاهد المعجزة فوقع في قلبه صدق النبي عليه السلام) فهو مكلف بتحصيل ذلك اختياراً، بل صرح هذا القائل بأن العلم بالنبوة الحاصل من المعجزات حدسي ربما يقع في القلب من غير اختيار ولا ينضم إليه التصديق الاختياري المأمور به وكل هذا موضع تأمل .
Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi said in Tabstrat al-Adilla: The absence of knowledge (ilm) does not necessitate the absence of tasdiq. For we have believed in the angels, the books, and the messengers, but we do not know them by their individual identities. And the obstinate ones (mu'anidun) know but do not tasdiq, as God Almighty said: 'Those to whom We gave the Book' (2). So this indicates the disjunction (infikak) of tasdiq from knowledge and knowledge from tasdiq. For this reason, faith (iman) was not considered knowledge (ma'rifa), according to the view of Jahm ibn Safwan. Fifth: That what was mentioned of considering choice (ikhtiyar) in the lexical tasdiq, and that what occurs without acquisition (kasb) and choice is not faith, indicates that the tasdiq of the angels regarding what was cast to them, of the prophets regarding what was revealed to them, and of the believers regarding what they heard from the Prophet (peace be upon him) is all acquired by choice. And that whoever obtains this meaning without acquisition, like one who witnesses a miracle and thus the truthfulness of the Prophet (peace be upon him) occurs in his heart, is obligated to acquire that by choice. Rather, this speaker explicitly said that the knowledge of prophethood obtained from miracles is intuitive (hadsī), perhaps occurring in the heart without choice, and the commanded optional tasdiq is not joined to it. And all of this is a place for reflection.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the nature of tasdiq. It begins by quoting Abu al-Mu'in al-Nasafi from his work Tabstrat al-Adilla. Al-Nasafi argues that the absence of knowledge does not imply the absence of tasdiq, because believers have tasdiq in angels, books, and messengers without knowing them individually. Conversely, obstinate unbelievers know the truth but do not tasdiq, as the Quran indicates (those given the Book). This shows a disjunction between tasdiq and knowledge. Therefore, faith is not identified with knowledge, contra Jahm ibn Safwan. Then the author presents a fifth point: The earlier discussion about considering choice in the linguistic meaning of tasdiq, and that what occurs without acquisition and choice is not faith, implies that the tasdiq of angels, prophets, and believers is all acquired by choice. Even one who witnesses a miracle and has the truthfulness of the Prophet occur in his heart is still obligated to acquire that tasdiq by choice. The author mentions that this speaker (likely a reference to a previous scholar) explicitly states that knowledge of prophethood obtained from miracles is intuitive and may occur without choice, yet the commanded optional tasdiq is not necessarily joined to it. The author concludes that all this calls for reflection.

علم
انفكاك
معرفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Some people think that faith is simply knowledge or intellectual conviction.
Correction: The text shows that tasdiq and knowledge can exist independently; faith requires tasdiq, which is not reducible to knowledge.

Checkpoint
According to the text, what does the example of obstinate unbelievers demonstrate?
A) That knowledge always leads to tasdiq
B) That tasdiq can exist without knowledge
C) That knowledge can exist without tasdiq
D) That tasdiq and knowledge are the same

Key Takeaway
Tasdiq and knowledge are not the same; one can exist without the other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Tasdiq Requires Choice and Acquisition
The author asserts the necessity of choice in tasdiq for all beings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that true tasdiq (and thus faith) must be acquired through choice and acquisition, and even those who witness miracles must make a voluntary act of tasdiq.

Core Idea
Faith requires voluntary choice; even miracles do not automatically produce faith.

The author now turns to the role of choice and acquisition in tasdiq. Building on the earlier definition of tasdiq as involving choice, he explains that the tasdiq of angels, prophets, and believers is all acquired by choice. Even someone who witnesses a miracle and gains intuitive knowledge of prophethood is still obligated to voluntarily affirm that truth. This reinforces that faith is a personal, intentional act.

These examples show that even the highest beings acquire tasdiq through choice.
3
Analyze the miracle witness case
The author addresses someone who sees a miracle and gains intuitive knowledge (hadsī). Why is this not enough? What is the obligation?
The intuitive knowledge may occur without choice, but commanded tasdiq requires voluntary act.
4
Reflect on the conclusion

It suggests the argument is presented but may require further contemplation.

Objection and Answer: Taslim and Tasdiq Are Synonymous
Objection and answer: defends that taslim is not additional to tasdiq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why later scholars who claimed taslim is additional to tasdiq were mistaken, and how the Salaf's interpretation supports the unity of the two concepts.

Core Idea
Taslim is not a separate component of faith; it is synonymous with tasdiq.

In this passage, the author addresses an objection that taslim (submission) is something additional to tasdiq (affirmation). The objector cites Quranic verses and the consensus of the Companions. The author's response clarifies that taslim is not additional but synonymous, as shown by the Persian translations used by the early Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Carefully read the objector's claim that tasdiq and taslim are the same and their Quranic evidence.
Note the two Quranic verses cited.
2
Read the author's answer
Read the author's response, which explains the mistake of later scholars.
The author defends the unity of the two concepts.
3
Analyze the Persian synonyms
Look at the Persian words quoted from the Salaf: they all mean 'believing' or 'accepting', showing taslim is not additional.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider why this matters: it prevents misunderstanding about the pillars of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : لا شك أن المقصود بالتصديق والتسليم واحد، والتصريح بذلك من أكابر الصحابة وعلماء الأمة وارد. وفي قوله تعالى : فلا وربك لا يؤمنون حتى يحكموك فيما شجر بينهم ثم لا يجدوا في أنفسهم حرجاً مما قضيت ويسلموا تسليماً) (۱). عليه ،شاهد، وإن أمكنت مناقشته وبقوله تعالى : ( وما زادهم إلا إيماناً وتسليماً) (٢). مجادلة . ففي اتحاد المفهوم لاغير . فما بال أقوام شددوا النكير، أو أكثروا المدافعة على من قال بذلك من المتأخرين ونسبوه إلى اختراع مذهب في الإسلام وزيادة ركن في الإيمان . قلنا : لأنه كان يزعم أولاً أن التسليم أمر زائد على التصديق الذي اعتبره العلماء لم ينكشف على من قبله من الأذكياء، واعترف بأنه إنما اطلع عليه بعد حين من الدهر وصدر من العمر مع أن السلف قد صرحوا بأن المراد به ما يعبر عنه في الفارسية بكرويدن و باورداشتن و بذيرفتن واراست کوي .داشتن . وأنه لا يكفي
If it is said: There is no doubt that the meaning of tasdiq and taslim (submission) is one, and the explicit statement of that is reported from the senior Companions and scholars of the Ummah. And in the saying of the Almighty: 'But no, by your Lord, they will not believe until they make you judge in what disputes arise among them, then find no discomfort in their hearts from what you have decided and submit fully (taslim)' (1) there is evidence, even if it can be objected. And by His saying: 'And it increased them only in faith and submission (taslim)' (2) there is an argument. So it is only in the unity of the concept. So what is the matter with some people who severely reproach or increase defense against those among the later scholars who said that, and attribute to them inventing a school in Islam and adding a pillar in faith? We say: Because he first claimed that taslim is something additional to tasdiq, which the scholars considered, and that it was not revealed to those before him among the intelligent, and he admitted that he only became aware of it after some time and age, whereas the Salaf explicitly stated that what is meant by it is what is expressed in Persian as 'garoyīdan (accepting), bāwar dāshtan (believing), biżīrīftan (accepting), arāst kardan (decorating?) dāshtan'. And that it does not suffice.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage presents another objection (فإن قيل) and answer (قلنا). The objection states that it is beyond doubt that tasdiq and taslim (submission) are the same in meaning, and this is explicitly reported from senior Companions and scholars. The objector provides Quranic evidence: from Surah al-Nisa (4:65) which mentions 'submitting fully' after arbitration, and from Surah al-Ahzab (33:22) which mentions 'faith and submission' as increasing. He argues that the concept is unified, so why do some people strongly oppose those later scholars who say they are identical, accusing them of innovation and adding a pillar of faith? The author's answer explains the reason: that scholar first claimed that taslim is something additional to tasdiq, which the scholars (earlier) had not noticed, and he admitted that he only discovered it late in life. However, the Salaf have explicitly stated that the meaning of taslim in Persian is expressed by words like 'garoyīdan' (accepting), 'bāwar dāshtan' (believing), 'biżīrīftan' (accepting), and 'arāst kardan dāshtan' (perhaps meaning 'to arrange' or 'to adorn with holding'), and that this (taslim) does not suffice alone. So the author defends that taslim is not an additional component but synonymous with tasdiq.

Key Terms
تصديق
تسليم
إيمان
كرويدن
باورداشتن
بذيرفتن
اراست کوي داشتن

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That taslim is an additional required component of faith beyond tasdiq.
Correction: Taslim is synonymous with tasdiq; it is not an extra element. The Salaf used Persian synonyms to show they are the same.

Checkpoint

B) He rejects it and says the terms are synonymous
C) He says it is different but not additional
D) He says the claim is true for modern scholars

Key Takeaway
Taslim is not an extra pillar of faith; it is synonymous with tasdiq as confirmed by the Salaf.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Faith Requires Choice and Acquisition
The author argues that tasdiq must be acquired by choice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why faith (iman) must be an act of choice and acquisition, not merely knowledge or intuitive certainty.

Core Idea
Faith is not knowledge; it is a chosen affirmation that must be acquired.

In this passage, the author presents a fifth argument that faith requires choice. He distinguishes tasdiq from knowledge and argues that even the certainty of prophets and angels is acquired by choice. This challenges the view that witnessing miracles automatically produces faith.

Guided Path
1
Understand the separation of tasdiq from knowledge
The author begins by stating that tasdiq and knowledge can be separated, which is why faith is not mere knowledge. Notice how he contrasts his view with Jahm ibn Safwan.
2
Trace the argument for choice in all tasdiq
The fifth point applies the principle that tasdiq without choice is not faith. This means angels, prophets, and believers all acquire their tasdiq by choice. Identify how the author extends this to the case of miracle witnesses.
3
Reflect on the implications
The author mentions a view that knowledge from miracles is intuitive and may lack the commanded choice-based tasdiq. He finds this debatable. Consider how this argument relates to personal faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فدل على انفكاك التصديق عن العلم والعلم عن التصديق. ولهذا لم يجعل الإيمان معرفة على ما ذهب إليه جهم بن صفوان. الخامس: أن ما ذكر من اعتبار الاختيار في نفس التصديق اللغوي، وكون الحاصل بلا كسب واختيار ليس بإيمان يدل على أن تصديق الملائكة بما ألقى عليهم، والأنبياء بما أوحي إليهم، والمصدقين بما سمعوا من النبي عليه السلام كله مكتسب بالاختيار. وأن من حصل له هذا المعنى بلا كسب كمن شاهد المعجزة فوقع في قلبه صدق النبي عليه السلام فهو مكلف بتحصيل ذلك اختياراً، بل صرح هذا القائل بأن العلم بالنبوة الحاصل من المعجزات حدسي ربما يقع في القلب من غير اختيار ولا ينضم إليه التصديق الاختياري المأمور به، وكل هذا موضع تأمل.
Thus it indicates the separation of tasdiq (affirmation) from knowledge and knowledge from tasdiq. For this reason, faith (iman) is not made mere knowledge as Jahm ibn Safwan held. The fifth: That what was mentioned of considering choice in the linguistic tasdiq itself, and that what occurs without acquisition and choice is not faith, indicates that the tasdiq of the angels to what was cast upon them, and the prophets to what was revealed to them, and the believers to what they heard from the Prophet (peace be upon him) is all acquired by choice. And that one for whom this meaning occurs without acquisition, like one who witnesses a miracle and certainty of the Prophet (peace be upon him) falls into his heart, is obligated to acquire that by choice. Rather, this speaker explicitly stated that knowledge of prophethood obtained from miracles is intuitive (hadsī), perhaps occurring in the heart without choice, and the commanded choice-based tasdiq is not joined to it. All of this is subject to reflection.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage presents a fifth argument in a series about the nature of faith (iman). The author begins by stating that the previous discussion has shown that tasdiq (affirmation) can be separated from knowledge and vice versa, which is why faith is not merely knowledge as the Jahmiyyah claim. The fifth point argues that choice (ikhtiyār) is essential to the linguistic meaning of tasdiq, and what occurs without acquisition (kasb) and choice is not faith. This implies that even the tasdiq of angels, prophets, and ordinary believers is all acquired by choice. The author then extends the argument: if someone, like a miracle witness, has certainty fall into his heart without choice, he is still obligated to acquire faith by choice. The author criticizes the view that knowledge from miracles is intuitive and may occur without choice, and that the commanded choice-based tasdiq is not joined to it. He concludes all this is debatable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that intuitive knowledge from miracles alone constitutes faith without need for choice.
Correction: The author argues that such knowledge is not sufficient; one must acquire choice-based tasdiq as commanded.

Checkpoint
What does the fifth point conclude about the tasdiq of angels and prophets?
A) It is purely intuitive and without choice.
B) It is all acquired by choice.
C) It is the same as knowledge.
D) It is not necessary for faith.

Key Takeaway
Faith is not merely knowledge or intuitive certainty; it must be an acquired, choice-based affirmation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel a surge of certainty about Allah or the Prophet, do you treat that feeling as faith, or do you actively choose to affirm it and act upon it? Where have you mistaken passive certainty for active faith?
?
The passage says even prophets and angels acquire tasdiq by choice. If they must choose, what does that mean for the effort you must invest? What are you choosing today to grow your faith beyond what comes naturally?
?
Think of a time you were confronted with a truth about Islam but did not act on it. Was that because you were waiting for a feeling, or because you failed to make a choice? What will you choose now to turn that knowledge into faith?

The Objection to Separating Tasdiq and Taslim
The author presents the objection and then lists the first two negative consequences of the opposing view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objector's argument that tasdiq and taslim are synonymous and the first two problematic consequences of the opposing view as presented by the author.

Core Idea
Claiming taslim is additional can imply earlier scholars were ignorant of faith.

This lesson begins with an objection: some argue that tasdiq and taslim are exactly the same, citing Quranic verses and statements of the Salaf. They criticize later scholars who separate them as innovators. The author responds by exposing the troubling implications of their view. We will first examine the objection and then the first two consequences: that it implies ignorance of earlier scholars, and that it abandons the common term tasdiq, causing confusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Note the Quranic verses cited and the claim of unity.
The objector uses strong language, accusing later scholars of inventing a new doctrine.
2
Identify the first consequence
The author responds with 'قلنا'. The first consequence is that the opponent admitted discovering taslim later, implying earlier scholars and even he himself were ignorant of true faith.
This is a serious accusation of arrogance.
3
Identify the second consequence
The second consequence is that the opponent abandoned the term tasdiq, leading people to think tasdiq and taslim are distinct, and causing extremists to detest one term.
This creates division and confusion.
4
Reflect on the harm
Consider why these consequences are damaging. How does the opponent's position undermine respect for earlier scholars and create sectarian tension?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: لا شك أن المقصود بالتصديق والتسليم واحد، والتصريح بذلك من أكابر الصحابة وعلماء الأمة وارد. وفي قوله تعالى: {فلا وربك لا يؤمنون حتى يحكموك فيما شجر بينهم ثم لا يجدوا في أنفسهم حرجاً مما قضيت ويسلموا تسليماً} عليه شاهد، وإن أمكنت مناقشته ومجادلة. وبقوله تعالى: {وما زادهم إلا إيماناً وتسليماً}. ففي اتحاد المفهوم لا غير. فما بال أقوام شددوا النكير، أو أكثروا المدافعة على من قال بذلك من المتأخرين ونسبوه إلى اختراع مذهب في الإسلام وزيادة ركن في الإيمان. قلنا: لأنه كان يزعم أولاً أن التسليم أمر زائد على التصديق الذي اعتبره العلماء، لم ينكشف على من قبله من الأذكياء، واعترف بأنه إنما اطلع عليه بعد حين من الدهر وصدر من العمر، مع أن السلف قد صرحوا بأن المراد به ما يعبر عنه في الفارسية بكرويدن وباورداشتن وبذيرفتن واراست كوي داشتن، وأنه لا يكفي مجرد المعرفة لحصولها لبعض الكفار على ما تلونا من الآيات، فكاد يفضي ذلك إلى نسبة نفسه مدة من الزمان، وكثير من السلف إلى الجهل بحقيقة الإيمان وإلى الإصرار على أنه لا بد من أمر وراء التصديق والإقرار. ولأنه اتخذ لفظ التصديق مهجوراً مع كونه في بين الأنام مشهوراً وعلى وجه الأيام مذكوراً، وبنى الأمر كله على لفظ التسليم بحيث اعتقد كثير من العوام بل الخواص أنهما معنيان مختلفان قد يجتمعان وقد يفترقان، لاحظ لأهل التصديق دون التسليم من الإيمان، وربما يرى الواحد من غلاة الفريقين وجهلة القبيلين يشمئز من أحد اللفظين، ولا يكتفي بأن يكون التصديق والتسليم مذهبين، ولأنه اعتبر في التسليم تحقيقات وتدقيقات لم تخطر ببال الكثير من المسلمين، بل لا يفهمها إلا الأذكياء من أئمة الدين، فاتخذها جهلة العوام ذريعة إلى تكفير الناس، وتجهيل الخواص، حتى استفتوه في شأن بعض رؤساء الدين وعلماء المسلمين والمهرة من المحققين فأفتى بكفره بناء على أنه أنكر بعض ما أورده هو في تحقيق الإيمان، مع أنك إذا تحققت فبعض منازعاتهما لفظي وبعضها اجتهادي، إلى غير ذلك من أمور قصد بها صلاح الدين، وقمع الجاحدين، لكنها أدت إلى ما أدت وأفضت إلى ما أفضت لما أنه ترك الأرفق إلى الأوفق، والأليق إلى الأوثق، ولا عليه، فإنه قد بذل الجهد في إحياء مراسم الدين وإعلاء لواء المسلمين، جزاه الله خير الجزاء عن أهل اليقين وأعلى درجته يوم اللقاء في عليين.
If it is said: There is no doubt that the intended meaning of tasdiq and taslim (submission) is one, and explicit statements to that effect from the senior Companions and scholars of the nation are transmitted. In Allah's saying: {But no, by your Lord, they will not [truly] believe until they make you judge concerning that over which they dispute among themselves and then find within themselves no discomfort from what you have judged and submit in [full, true] submission} there is a witness, even if it can be debated and argued. And by His saying: {And it increased them only in faith and submission}. So the concept is one, nothing else. Why then do some people severely criticize or argue vehemently against those among the later scholars who said this, and attribute to them inventing a new doctrine in Islam and adding a pillar of faith? We say: Because he firstly claimed that taslim is something additional to the tasdiq recognized by scholars, unknown to those before him among the intelligent, and admitted that he only discovered it after some time from his life and a portion of his age, while the Salaf had explicitly stated that what is meant by it is expressed in Persian as 'karoīdan wa bāwar dāshtan wa bērafṭan wa ārāst kuī dāshtan', and that mere knowledge is insufficient because it occurs in some disbelievers as we have recited from the verses. That almost led to attributing to himself for a period of time and to many of the Salaf ignorance of the true nature of faith, and to insisting that there must be something beyond tasdiq and verbal confession. And because he abandoned the term tasdiq while it was famous among people and mentioned throughout the days, and based everything on the term taslim such that many commoners, even the elite, believed that they are two different meanings that may come together or separate, with no share of faith for the people of tasdiq without taslim, and perhaps one of the extremists of the two groups and the ignorant of the two tribes would detest one of the two terms, and he was not satisfied with tasdiq and taslim being two schools. And because he introduced in taslim investigations and subtleties that had never crossed the minds of many Muslims, but only the intelligent from the imams of religion understand them, so the ignorant commoners took them as a pretext for excommunicating people and declaring the elite ignorant, until they consulted him about some leaders of religion and scholars of Muslims and skillful investigators, and he issued a fatwa of their disbelief based on their denial of some of what he presented in his investigation of faith, although if you investigate, some of their disputes are verbal and some are ijtihādī. This is in addition to other matters intended for the reform of religion and suppression of the deniers, but they led to what they led and resulted in what they resulted, because he left the more gentle for the more appropriate, and the more fitting for the more reliable. No blame on him, for he exerted effort in reviving the rites of religion and raising the banner of Muslims. May Allah reward him with the best reward from the people of certainty, and raise his rank on the day of meeting in the 'Illiyyūn.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer structure. The objector claims that tasdiq and taslim are synonymous, citing Quranic verses and the usage of the Salaf, and criticizes those who separate them as innovators. The author responds (قلنا) by detailing the problematic consequences of the opposing view: (1) the opponent admitted he discovered the additional meaning late, implying earlier scholars were ignorant; (2) he abandoned the common term tasdiq, causing confusion among people who now think they are distinct and may hate one term; (3) he introduced overly subtle investigations that led ignorant people to excommunicate others, even leading him to declare some leading scholars disbelievers. The author then notes that many of these disputes are verbal or ijtihādī, and despite the unintended negative outcomes, the person intended good, so he is excused and even rewarded for his efforts.

Key Terms
تصديق
تسليم
إيمان
سلف
كفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first negative consequence the author mentions?
A) Confusion among commoners about the terms
B) The opponent accused earlier scholars of ignorance
C) The opponent rejected Quranic verses
D) The opponent added a new pillar to Islam

Key Takeaway
The objector's claim that taslim is not additional implies that those who believe otherwise are ignorant, which is harmful and disrespectful to earlier scholarship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed someone's theological view as an innovation without first examining the consequences of your own position? This lesson shows how an objection can backfire. How can you ensure your own criticisms are free from arrogance and division?
?
The objector accused later scholars of inventing a new doctrine. When you encounter a new perspective on a religious issue, do you rush to defend the 'orthodox' view, or do you pause to consider whether your own understanding might be incomplete? What does this reveal about your heart?
?
The author points out that abandoning the term 'tasdiq' in favor of 'taslim' caused confusion and division. Is there a word or phrase in your faith practice that you hold so tightly that it distances you from others who use different terms? How can you seek unity without compromising truth?

The Consequences of Subtlety in Defining Taslim
The author details the harmful effects of subtle theological investigations and offers a final charitable judgment.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how excessive subtlety in defining taslim led to takfir and division, and the author's conclusion that many disputes are verbal or ijtihadi.

Core Idea
Overcomplicating faith can lead to unjust excommunication.

In this continuation of the author's response, he turns to the third and most severe consequence: the opponent introduced overly sophisticated investigations into taslim that only a few understand. Ignorant followers used these to excommunicate other Muslims, even leading the opponent himself to declare some scholars disbelievers. The author then notes that many of these disputes are linguistic or matters of ijtihad, and despite the negative outcomes, the opponent had good intentions.

Guided Path
1
Read the third consequence
Read the passage about the opponent's subtle investigations. Notice that only a few intelligent imams can understand them.
The author uses 'تحقيقات وتدقيقات' to describe excessive refinement.
2
Identify the misuse by ignorant followers
The ignorant commoners used these subtleties as a pretext to excommunicate people and declare the elite ignorant.
This is a grave consequence.
3
Note the opponent's own fatwa
He was consulted about leading scholars and issued a fatwa of disbelief based on his definitions.
This shows the practical harm.
4
Understand the author's corrective
The author states that many disputes are verbal (لفظي) or ijtihadi (اجتهادي), not fundamental.
This reduces the severity.
5
Reflect on the final judgment
Despite the negative outcomes, the author excuses the opponent because of his good intentions and efforts for Islam.
A lesson in charity.

Faith and Disbelief

The Third Station: Actions Are Not Part of Faith's Essence
The author gives four proofs that actions are not part of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the arguments that actions are not part of the reality of faith (iman), based on linguistic, scriptural, and logical evidence.

Core Idea
Actions are commanded results of faith, not its essence.

In this lesson, we examine the third station of the discussion on faith. The author presents four clear proofs that actions (a'māl) are not included in the definition of iman. By understanding these proofs, we see that faith is fundamentally affirmation (tasdiq), and deeds are separate commanded duties. The passage draws on Quranic verses and logical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Let the author's rhythm come through before interpreting.
The passage is compact; each proof follows the word 'و' (and).
2
Understand the linguistic argument
The author states that faith (iman) is a name for tasdiq (affirmation) and there is no linguistic transference (naql) to include actions. This means the word's original meaning does not extend to actions.
Linguistic analysis is key in usul al-din.
3
Reflect on the deathbed argument
Faith does not benefit at the moment of witnessing punishment (at death), and no action can help then. This shows faith and action are separate; action cannot substitute for faith.
4
Consider the commands to believers
The author cites verses commanding believers to fast and not to put themselves forward. If faith included actions, commanding believers would be redundant; the command implies faith is already present and actions are required separately.
This logical inference is called 'istidlal' (deduction).
5
Analyze the Quranic pairing
Verses like 'Those who have believed and done righteous deeds' pair faith and actions as two distinct things, proving they are not the same.
This is direct textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: المقام الثالث. إن الأعمال غير داخلة في حقيقة الإيمان لما ثبت أنه اسم للتصديق، ولا نقل، وأنه لا ينفع عند معاينة العذاب ولا عمل، وأن المؤمن قد يؤمر وينهى مثل: {يا أيها الذين آمنوا كتب عليكم الصيام} و {يا أيها الذين آمنوا لا تقدموا} وللنصوص الدالة على أنهما أمران متغايران مثل: {الذين آمنوا وعملوا الصالحات}.
He said: The third station. Verily actions are not included in the reality of faith (iman) because it has been established that it (faith) is a name for tasdiq (affirmation), and no (linguistic) transference (naql), and that it (faith) does not benefit at the time of witnessing punishment, and no action (then), and that the believer may be commanded and forbidden, like: {O you who have believed, decreed upon you is fasting} and {O you who have believed, do not put yourselves forward}, and due to the texts indicating that they (faith and action) are two different things, like: {Those who have believed and done righteous deeds}.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage introduces the third station (maqām) of the discussion, where the author argues that actions (a'māl) are not part of the essence of faith (īmān). He provides four pieces of evidence: (1) It is established that the word 'faith' is a name for tasdiq (affirmation) alone, and there is no linguistic transference (naql) that would extend it to actions; (2) Faith does not benefit at the time of witnessing punishment (i.e., at death), and no action can help then either; (3) A believer is commanded and forbidden (e.g., to fast, to not put himself forward), which would be odd if faith included actions—otherwise commanding believers would be redundant; (4) Texts (e.g., Quranic verses) distinguish between 'those who have believed' and 'those who have done righteous deeds', showing they are two different things.

Key Terms
إيمان
عمل
تصديق
نقل
آيات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Actions are an essential part of faith; faith without deeds is incomplete.
Correction: Faith is purely affirmation (tasdiq) in the heart; actions are separate commanded duties, as shown by linguistic and scriptural evidence.

Checkpoint
What is one of the proofs given that actions are not part of faith?
A) Actions are required for salvation.
B) The believer is commanded and forbidden, implying faith is separate.
C) The Quran repeatedly mentions both together.
D) The Salaf defined faith as including actions.

Key Takeaway
Faith (iman) is affirmation (tasdiq) alone; actions are separate commanded results, as proven by linguistic, logical, and scriptural evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you secretly measure your faith by your deeds, feeling that when you sin your iman is less? How does this lesson's clear distinction between faith (tasdiq) and actions challenge that feeling? What will you do this week to reaffirm that your faith is solely based on your heart's affirmation, not your performance?
?
The source says faith does not benefit at the moment of punishment, and no action can help then. If you were to die right now, would you be relying on your deeds or on the affirmation in your heart? How does this shift your focus for today's actions?
?
You are commanded to act (like fasting and not putting yourself forward) precisely because you already have faith. Are you treating your worship as a way to earn faith or as a grateful response to the faith you have? From now on, how will you remind yourself that your deeds are commanded results, not the foundation of your salvation?

Overemphasis on Taslim and the Neglect of Tasdiq
Critique of elevating taslim over tasdiq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a scholar's overemphasis on taslim (submission) over tasdiq (assent) led to confusion about the nature of faith and created division.

Core Idea
Elevating one word over another can distort the understanding of faith.

This passage from al-Maqasid criticizes a scholar who, in his zeal to define faith correctly, abandoned the widely accepted term tasdiq and built everything on taslim. The result was widespread confusion among commoners and even elites, who began to think tasdiq and taslim are completely different concepts. Let's examine the author's critique.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the problem
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that the author starts by pointing out that mere knowledge (ma'rifa) is insufficient, and then criticizes the scholar for abandoning the term tasdiq in favor of taslim.
The passage uses 'tasdiq' and 'taslim' as key terms.
2
Understand the confusion caused
The author states that many commoners and even elites came to believe that tasdiq and taslim are two different meanings that may come together or separate. This led to the idea that one could have tasdiq without taslim and still have faith.
3
Reflect on the extremism mentioned
The author mentions that extremists from both groups abhor one of the two words, refusing to accept that both terms are valid schools. This shows how linguistic preference can lead to sectarianism.
Notice the author's disapproval of such extremism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجرد المعرفة لحصولها لبعض الكفار على ما تلونا من الآيات، فكاد يفضي ذلك إلى نسبة نفسه مدة من الزمان، وكثير من السلف إلى الجهل بحقيقة الإيمان وإلى الإصرار على أنه لا بد من أمر وراء التصديق والإقرار . ولأنه اتخذ لفظ التصديق مهجوراً مع كونه في بين الأنام مشهوراً وعلى وجه الأيام مذكوراً ، وبنى الأمر كله على لفظ التسليم بحيث اعتقد كثير من العوام بل الخواص أنهما معنيان مختلفان قد يجتمعان وقد يفترقان، لاحظ لأهل التصديق دون التسليم من الإيمان، وربما يرى الواحد من غلاة الفريقين وجهلة القبيلين يشمئز من أحد اللفظين، ولا يكتفي بأن يكون التصديق والتسليم مذهبين ، ولأنه اعتبر في التسليم تحقيقات وتدقيقات لم تخطر ببال الكثير من المسلمين، بل لا يفهمها إلا الأذكياء من أئمة الدين ، فاتخذها جهلة العوام ذريعة إلى تكفير الناس، وتجهيل الخواص، حتى استفتوه في شأن بعض رؤساء الدين وعلماء المسلمين والمهرة من المحققين فأفتى بكفره بناء على أنه أنكر بعض ما أورده هو في تحقيق الإيمان، مع أنك إذا تحققت فبعض منازعاتهما لفظي وبعضها اجتهادي، إلى غير ذلك من أمور قصد بها صلاح الدين، وقمع الجاحدين ، لكنها أدت إلى ما أدت وأفضت إلى ما أفضت لما أنه ترك الأرفق إلى الأوفق ، والأليق إلى الأوثق ، ولا عليه ، فإنه قد بذل الجهد في إحياء مراسم الدين وإعلاء لواء المسلمين، جزاه الله خير الجزاء عن أهل اليقين وأعلى درجته يوم اللقاء في عليين .
Mere knowledge because it is obtained by some disbelievers according to what we have recited of the verses, so that almost led to attributing himself for a period of time, and many of the Salaf, to ignorance of the reality of faith, and to insisting that there must be something beyond assent (tasdiq) and confession (iqrar). And because he made the word tasdiq abandoned while it is well-known among people and mentioned on the face of days, and he built the entire matter on the word taslim (submission) so that many commoners, rather even the elite, believed that they are two different meanings that may come together and may separate, with no share for the people of tasdiq without taslim in faith. And perhaps one of the extremists of the two groups and the ignorant of the two tribes may abhor one of the two words, and is not satisfied that tasdiq and taslim are two schools. And because he considered in taslim verifications and precisions that did not occur to the minds of many Muslims; rather, only the intelligent among the leading scholars of the religion understand them. Then the ignorant commoners took them as a means to declare people disbelievers (takfir) and to declare the elite ignorant. Until they sought a fatwa from him regarding some of the leaders of the religion, scholars of the Muslims, and skilled investigators, and he gave a fatwa of his disbelief based on the fact that he denied some of what he himself had presented in the investigation of faith, while if you investigate, some of their disputes are verbal and some are ijtihadi. And other matters intended for the reform of the religion and suppression of deniers, but they led to what they led and resulted in what they resulted, because he left what is more fitting for what is more appropriate, and what is more suitable for what is more trustworthy. No blame on him, for he exerted effort in reviving the rites of the religion and raising the banner of the Muslims. May Allah reward him with the best reward for the people of certainty and elevate his rank on the Day of Meeting in the highest paradise.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage criticizes an unnamed scholar (likely al-Ghazali or a similar figure) who, in the author's view, overemphasized the term taslim (submission) at the expense of tasdiq (assent) in defining faith (iman). The author argues that this led to confusion, with many people thinking tasdiq and taslim are distinct meanings, and that some extremists abhor one term or the other. The scholar's intricate discussions on taslim were used by ignorant people to declare others disbelievers (takfir), even leading to a fatwa of disbelief against a prominent scholar. The author points out that many of these disputes are either verbal or ijtihadi (based on independent reasoning), implying they should not lead to takfir. He then excuses the criticized scholar by acknowledging his good intentions and efforts for the religion, praying for Allah's reward.

Key Terms
تصديق
تسليم
إيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That tasdiq and taslim are entirely separate components of faith, and that one can have faith without both.
Correction: The author implies that tasdiq and taslim are two terms for the same reality, and that overemphasizing one over the other leads to error.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was the consequence of the scholar abandoning the word tasdiq and building everything on taslim?
A) People understood faith more clearly.
B) Many commoners and elites believed tasdiq and taslim are two different meanings.
C) The scholar was universally praised.
D) The term tasdiq became more popular.

Key Takeaway
Overemphasizing a single theological term can cause unnecessary division and confusion about the fundamentals of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever preferred a certain word or phrase in your religious practice to the point of dismissing others? What does your preference reveal about your heart, and how might it affect those around you? Take one specific term you cling to and ask yourself: would you be willing to also honor an alternative term if it leads to greater unity?
?
The passage says even the elite were confused. In what ways might your own theological biases or scholarly preferences be causing confusion for others—perhaps without you realizing it? Commit today to re-examine one area where you have been quick to dismiss a different expression of faith.
?
If you were to replace the word 'taslim' with a term you personally prefer (like 'obedience' or 'surrender'), would you still be able to accept and respect someone who uses 'tasdiq' as their primary term? If not, what does that say about your own understanding of faith? Will you actively practice affirming both terms as valid schools, as the author suggests?

The Danger of Takfir and the Author's Balanced Conclusion
Critique of takfir and balanced evaluation of the scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how excessive theological precision can lead to unjust takfir and how the author balances criticism with appreciation.

Core Idea
Theological disputes should not lead to declaring others disbelievers.

Continuing his critique, the author shows how the scholar's intricate investigations into taslim were used by ignorant people as a pretext to declare others disbelievers. The passage ends with a remarkable example of a fatwa of disbelief against a leading scholar, followed by the author's measured evaluation. Let's see how the author navigates between defending orthodoxy and avoiding extremism.

Guided Path
1
Read about the intricate verifications
Read how the scholar introduced deep investigations (tahqiqat) that only the intelligent could understand. This created a body of knowledge inaccessible to commoners.
These verifications were about the reality of taslim.
2
Identify the misuse by ignorant commoners
The ignorant commoners used these intricate ideas as a means to declare people disbelievers (takfir) and to declare the elite ignorant. This is a serious consequence of overcomplicating faith.
3
Examine the fatwa example
The commoners sought a fatwa from the scholar regarding a respected leader of the religion. The scholar gave a fatwa of disbelief because the leader denied some of his own findings about faith. The author comments that many of these disputes are either verbal (lafzi) or based on ijtihad.
This shows the danger of takfir based on nuanced theological opinions.
4
Reflect on the author's final judgment
The author acknowledges the scholar's good intentions—reviving the religion and suppressing deniers—but notes that he left the more fitting approach for the less fitting. Still, he prays for him. This balance is key.
The author does not fully condemn but rather offers a nuanced evaluation.

Mu'tazilite Proof from Quran 8:2 and Ash'ari Refutation
Mu'tazilite proof from Quran 8:2 and Ash'ari reply.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ash'ari school responds to the Mu'tazilite proof from Quran 8:2 by distinguishing between the essential definition of iman and its perfection.

Core Idea
Descriptions of perfect faith do not redefine the essence of iman.

The Mu'tazilites often used Quranic verses that describe believers' emotional and active responses to argue that iman includes more than inner conviction. In this second proof, they cite a verse about hearts trembling at the mention of Allah. The Ash'ari reply is concise: this verse describes the perfect believer, not the minimal reality of faith. This lesson unpacks that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the brevity: the proof is a single verse citation, and the reply is a single phrase.
2
Understand the Mu'tazilite proof
The Mu'tazilites argue that the verse describes believers as having trembling hearts, implying that iman includes emotional states and actions beyond mere tasdiq.
3
Analyze the Ash'ari reply
The author says 'Areed al-kamil' — what is intended is the perfect believer. This means the verse describes the ideal, not the essential definition (haqiqa).
This distinction is key to the Ash'ari position that iman is essentially tasdiq, and actions are its perfection.
4
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to see if you can apply the distinction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - إنما المؤمنون الذين إذا ذكر الله وجلت قلوبهم (٥) قلنا : أريد الكامل.
Second – 'The believers are only those who, when Allah is mentioned, their hearts tremble' (5) We said: What is intended is the perfect (believer).
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This is the second Mu'tazilite proof, citing the verse from Surah al-Anfal (8:2): 'The believers are only those who, when Allah is mentioned, their hearts tremble...' The Mu'tazilites likely use this verse to argue that iman includes emotional responses and actions (like trembling) that go beyond mere tasdiq. The author's brief reply is that this verse describes the 'perfect' (al-kamil) believer, i.e., the ideal state of faith, not the minimal reality (haqiqa) that is simply tasdiq. Thus, it does not prove that actions are part of the essential definition of iman; rather, it describes a praiseworthy quality of those who have already attained the reality of faith.

Key Terms
إيمان
كامل
وجل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Quranic descriptions of believers define the essential meaning of iman.
Correction: The Ash'ari school distinguishes between the essential reality (haqiqa) of iman and its perfection (kamal). Verses like 8:2 describe the latter.

Checkpoint

B) He says it refers to the perfect believer, not the minimal reality of iman.
C) He agrees but adds that actions are still not required.
D) He claims the verse is metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari reply to the Mu'tazilite proof from Quran 8:2 is that the verse describes the perfect believer, not the essential definition of iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

The Third Mu'tazilite Proof: Does 'Faith' Mean Prayer?
Third Mu'tazilite proof from verse on prayer direction, refuted as metaphorical.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazilites used the verse 'Allah would not waste your faith' to argue that iman includes actions, and why the Ash'aris dismissed it as metaphorical.

Core Idea
The Mu‘tazilite proof from the Jerusalem prayer verse fails because 'iman' there is figurative, not literal.

The debate over the definition of iman often turns on scriptural verses that seem to equate faith with actions. One such verse is Surah al-Baqarah 2:143, where the word 'iman' appears in a context about the change of qibla. The Mu'tazilites seized upon this as evidence that iman can mean prayer. In this lesson, we examine their argument and the Ash'ari response.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two parts: the Mu'tazilite proof and the Ash'ari reply.
The verse is cited with a footnote marker (4).
2
Understand the Mu'tazilite interpretation
The Mu'tazilites interpret 'iman' in the verse as 'prayer' (salat) towards Jerusalem. This supports their view that iman includes actions.
This interpretation relies on the context of the change of qibla.
3
Grasp the Ash'ari reply
The author calls this interpretation metaphorical (majaz). The real meaning is 'your assent (tasdiq) to the obligation of prayer' – i.e., Allah will not waste the reward for your belief in the obligation.
Thus, the verse does not prove that iman literally means action; it uses iman metonymically.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث - ( وما كان الله ليضيع إيمانكم ) (٤) أي صلاتكم إلى بيت المقدس . قلنا مجاز، والمراد تصديقكم بوجوبها .
Third – 'And Allah would never waste your faith' (4) meaning your prayer towards Jerusalem. We said: It is metaphorical (majaz), and what is meant is your assent (tasdiq) to its obligation.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This is the third Mu'tazilite proof, citing the verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:143): 'And Allah would never waste your faith.' The Mu'tazilites interpret 'iman' here as 'prayer' (salat) towards Jerusalem, based on the context that the direction of prayer was changed. This is a classic proof that iman can mean actions (prayer). The Ash'ari author replies that this is metaphorical (majaz). The real meaning is 'your tasdiq (assent) to the obligation of prayer' – i.e., Allah will not let the reward for your belief in the obligation of prayer be lost. Thus, the verse does not prove that iman literally means action; rather, it uses iman metonymically for the belief that gives rise to the action.

Key Terms
إيمان
صلاة
مجاز
تصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the verse proves the literal inclusion of actions in the definition of iman.
Correction: The author clarifies it is figurative (majaz) and refers to the underlying belief (tasdiq).

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari author, what does the word 'iman' in the verse 'Allah would never waste your faith' actually mean?
A) The action of prayer itself.
B) The assent (tasdiq) to the obligation of prayer.
C) Both the belief and the action combined.
D) The reward for prayer.

Key Takeaway
The verse does not support the Mu'tazilite definition of iman, as the term is used metaphorically; the real meaning is the belief in the obligation of prayer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a physical act of worship like prayer, do you ever catch yourself relying more on the outward action than on the inner conviction that it is an obligation from Allah? How can you strengthen the inner tasdiq (belief) behind your actions starting today?
?
If the verse about the change of qibla teaches that Allah rewards the belief behind the action, not just the action itself, then how should this change the way you evaluate your own worship? Will you begin examining your intentions more deeply right now?
?
The Mu'tazilites built an entire definition of faith on a single verse, but misunderstood its metaphorical nature. Where in your own life might you be building a wrong belief on a misunderstood text or experience? Are you willing to let go of that assumption today?

The First Mu'tazili Proof: Iman as 'Din'
The Mu'tazila present their claim that iman is transferred to actions, and the first proof using 'din'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first Mu'tazili argument that iman is transferred to actions through the term 'din', and the refutation that shows the term is ambiguous.

Core Idea
Calling iman 'din' does not prove it includes actions—the term can mean submission.

The Mu'tazila built their case that actions are part of iman on eight proofs. The first draws on the Quranic term 'din' (religion), which encompasses practices like prayer. But is this transfer of meaning sound? In this passage, we see both sides: their proof and the critical response that exposes its ambiguity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the Mu'tazila's opening concession and their claim of transfer (naql).
Notice they don't deny that iman is essentially attestation.
2
Identify the first proof
The Mu'tazila argue that iman is called 'din' in the Quran, and din includes actions like prayer. Locate the verse they cite and their reasoning.
Verse: 'That is the straight din' after mentioning prayer.
3
Examine the answer (al-jawab)
The refutation points out that 'that' could refer to sincerity or submission, not necessarily iman. It also says that 'the din with Allah is Islam' and that the equation of Islam and iman will be discussed later.
The answer does not reject the verse but offers alternative interpretations.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this refutation shows that linguistic or scriptural evidence must be interpreted carefully, especially when sectarian disputes arise.
This is a classic example of tafsir-based theological argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالت المعتزلة : نحن لا ننكر إطلاق الإيمان على التصديق بالأمور المخصوصة، لكنا ندعي نقله إلى الأعمال بوجوه : الأول - أنها الدين لقوله تعالى : وذلك الدين القيم ﴾ ( إشارة إلى المذكور من إقامة الصلاة، وغيرها. والدين المعتبر هو الإسلام لقوله تعالى : ( إن الدين عند الله الإسلام (٤) والإسلام هو الإيمان لما سيجيء . وأجيب بأنه يجوز أن يكون ذلك إشارة إلى الإخلاص أو التدين والانقياد ، وأن يراد أن الدين المعتبر عند الله دين الإسلام، وسنتكلم على كون الإسلام هو الإيمان .
And the Mu'tazila said: We do not deny the application of 'iman' to the specific matters of attestation, but we claim its transfer to actions by ways: The first: That it is 'din' because of His statement: 'That is the straight din' referring to what was mentioned of establishing prayer and others. And the considered din is Islam because of His statement: 'Indeed, the din with Allah is Islam' (4), and Islam is iman as will come. And it was answered that it is possible that that refers to sincerity or to religiosity and submission, and that it is intended that the considered din with Allah is the din of Islam, and we will discuss that Islam is iman.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage presents the first Mu'tazili argument that actions are part of iman. The Mu'tazila begin by stating their position: they do not deny that iman is essentially attestation, but they argue that the term has been transferred (nuqila) to include actions. They provide eight proofs; this is the first. Their first proof is that iman is called 'din' in the Quran, and din includes actions like prayer. They cite two verses: 'That is the straight religion' (after mentioning prayer) and 'Indeed, the religion with Allah is Islam.' They argue that Islam is iman (as will be explained). The answer (mujib) refutes by saying that the reference could be to sincerity (ikhlas) or to the general meaning of submission, and that the intended meaning is that the accepted religion is Islam. The author promises to discuss the equation of Islam and iman later.

Key Terms
إيمان
دين
إسلام
تصديق
نقل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the term 'din' in the verse necessarily refers to iman, so actions become part of iman.
Correction: The term 'din' is ambiguous; it can mean sincerity or submission in general, not necessarily iman. The refutation shows the proof is not decisive.

Checkpoint
What is the first proof presented by the Mu'tazila that iman includes actions?
A) They argue that iman is called 'salah' in the Quran
B) They argue that iman is called 'din' and din includes actions
C) They argue that iman is called 'huda' and huda implies guidance
D) They argue that iman is called 'taqwa' and taqwa includes deeds

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's first proof from 'din' is refuted by showing the term's ambiguity, demonstrating that proof requires more than lexical overlap.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read the verse 'That is the straight din', do you automatically assume it refers to iman? What does that reveal about how you approach the Quran? Are you willing to admit that your first impression might be incorrect? How will you train yourself to consider multiple interpretations before forming a firm belief?
?
This lesson shows that the Mu'tazila used a weak proof to support a position they already held. Have you ever defended a belief with a weak argument simply because it was convenient? What does that say about your attachment to truth? Will you commit to building your faith only on the strongest evidence, even if it challenges your assumptions?
?
The rebuttal points out that the same word 'din' can mean submission or sincerity. In your own life, are there terms like 'iman' or 'Islam' that you have defined too rigidly? What might you be missing about the richness of these concepts? How can you open your heart to deeper understandings from the Quran and Sunnah?
