The Verse of Trembling Hearts: Action or Attribute?
Mu'tazila cite verse, Ash'ari limits to perfect believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila used Quran 8:2 to argue for actions being part of iman and how the Ash'ari response limits the verse to perfect believers.

Core Idea
The verse describes perfect believers, not the essence of iman.

The Mu'tazila often turned to Quranic descriptions of believers to support their view that actions are intrinsic to faith. One key verse is Quran 8:2, which speaks of hearts trembling at the mention of Allah. In this short but precise passage, the commentator defuses the argument by clarifying the verse’s scope.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice its brevity: it is an objection-answer pair.
The number (5) is a footnote marker, not part of the verse.
2
Identify the Mu'tazila argument
The Mu'tazila cite the verse to claim that trembling hearts (a bodily action) is a necessary characteristic of believers, so actions must be part of iman.
They use the word 'innama' to imply exclusivity.
3
Understand the Ash'ari response
The response says 'the perfect [believer] is intended' (أريد الكامل). This means the verse refers to the highest degree of faith, not the minimal essence of iman.
The term 'kamil' refers to the believer who has both inner attestation and outward actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني - إنما المؤمنون الذين إذا ذكر الله وجلت قلوبهم (٥)  قلنا : أريد الكامل.
The second: 'The believers are only those who, when Allah is mentioned, their hearts tremble' (5). We said: The perfect [believer] is intended.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This is a short objection-answer pair. The Mu'tazila cite Quran 8:2, which describes believers as those whose hearts tremble when Allah is mentioned. They argue that this trembling is a bodily action, proving that actions are part of iman. The answer is concise: 'We said: the perfect [believer] is intended' (أريد الكامل). This means that the verse describes the complete or perfect believer who has both attestation and actions, not the minimal iman that is mere attestation. Thus, it does not refute that the essence of iman is attestation alone.

Key Terms
كامل
وجلت قلوبهم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'إنما المؤمنون...' applies to all believers equally, proving that actions are part of iman for everyone.
Correction: The verse actually describes the perfect believer (الكامل), not every believer. It highlights a high station of faith, not the minimal definition.

Checkpoint
How does the Ash'ari response refute the Mu'tazila use of the verse?
A) By denying the authenticity of the verse
B) By saying the verse refers to perfect believers, not all believers
C) By arguing that trembling is not an action
D) By claiming the verse is abrogated

Key Takeaway
The verse 'إنما المؤمنون...' describes perfect believers, not the minimal definition of iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the Quran recited, do you ever feel your heart tremble with awe? If not, what does that say about the state of your iman? What will you do today to cultivate that sensitivity?
?
This lesson shows that iman has levels—you could be a believer without being a 'perfect believer'. Have you ever settled for the minimum, content to simply say 'I believe' without striving for the heartfelt devotion this verse describes? What is one concrete change you will make this week to move toward that perfection?
?
The Mu'tazila wanted to make actions essential to iman; the Ash'ari response protects the mercy of Allah—that even imperfect believers are still believers. Do you secretly despise those whose faith is weak, forgetting that you yourself are not the perfect believer described in the verse? Ask forgiveness and resolve to help others grow rather than judge.

The Third Proof: Figurative Use of 'Iman' for Prayer
The Mu'tazila interpret 'iman' as prayer; the answer says it is figurative.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Mu'tazila misuse a Quranic verse to argue for actions being part of iman, and how the Ash'ari response clarifies the figurative usage.

Core Idea
The verse uses 'iman' figuratively, not literally for action.

In this lesson, we examine the third proof put forward by the Mu'tazila from Quran 2:143, where they interpret 'iman' as prayer. The Ash'ari response demonstrates that this is a figurative usage (majaz), preserving the literal meaning of iman as attestation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once. Then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: the Mu'tazila claim, then the response.
The verse number (4) is a footnote marker.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila claim
The Mu'tazila interpret 'iman' in the verse as prayer (salat) towards Jerusalem. They use this to argue that the word 'iman' can mean an action, supporting their view that actions are part of faith.
3
Grasp the Ash'ari refutation
The response states it is figurative (majaz). The real intended meaning is your attestation (tasdiq) of the obligation of that prayer. This preserves the literal meaning of iman as attestation.
Figurative usage does not change the core meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث - ( وما كان الله ليضيع إيمانكم ) (٤) أي صلاتكم إلى بيت المقدس . قلنا مجاز، والمراد تصديقكم بوجوبها .
The third: 'And Allah would never waste your iman' (4) meaning your prayer towards Jerusalem. We said: [It is] figurative, and what is intended is your attestation of its obligation.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
The Mu'tazila cite Quran 2:143, where 'iman' is interpreted by some as prayer (salat) towards Jerusalem. They take this as evidence that the word 'iman' can be used for actions. The answer rejects this by stating that it is a figurative usage (majaz). The real referent is the believers' attestation (tasdiq) of the obligation of that prayer. The literal meaning of 'iman' remains attestation, and the verse uses it figuratively to refer to the act of prayer that results from that attestation.

Key Terms
مجاز
تصديق
وجوب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse proves a literal transfer of 'iman' to prayer.
Correction: It is only a figurative usage (majaz); the literal meaning remains attestation.

Checkpoint
How do the Mu'tazila use the verse 'وما كان الله ليضيع إيمانكم' to argue for actions being part of iman?
A) They say the verse means that Allah will not waste their deeds
B) They interpret 'iman' as prayer, showing it is used for an action
C) They say 'iman' here means belief in the qibla
D) They argue that the verse proves iman increases and decreases

Key Takeaway
The verse 'wa ma kana Allahu li-yudi'a imanakum' is interpreted figuratively to refer to prayer, but the literal meaning of iman remains attestation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Mu'tazila used this verse to argue that actions are part of iman. When you look at your own practice, do you ever treat your prayers or other deeds as the measure of your faith? How does the Ash'ari response—that the verse is figurative and the true meaning is your inner attestation—expose any overreliance on external acts? What would it mean for you to focus more on your tasdiq today?
?
The verse speaks of Allah not wasting your 'iman', interpreted figuratively as prayer. Reflect: Have you ever felt that your good deeds (prayer, charity, fasting) could be 'wasted' if not accepted? How does knowing that the real iman is your attestation—something that cannot be lost by mere error in direction—change your sense of security in Allah's acceptance?
?
In this lesson, the Ash'ari say the intended meaning is 'your attestation of its obligation'. Is your obedience to Allah driven more by a deep inner conviction that this is true, or by habit and expectation? Take a moment: What is one obligation you perform today that you can consciously renew as an act of tasdiq?

The Fourth Proof: Highway Robber and Disgrace - Argument and Refutation
Mu'tazilite proof from robber's disgrace and its refutation by denying major premise

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazilite proof concerning the highway robber and the refutation by denying the major premise, learning how scriptural specificity can restrict a general claim.

Core Idea
Not everyone in Hell is eternally disgraced; the verse is specific to the Companions.

The Mu'tazila used the fate of a highway robber to argue that sin excludes a person from true faith. They built a syllogism with three Quranic verses. The answer challenges the major premise of that syllogism by showing that one of the verses applies only to a specific group, not to all believers. Let's examine the proof and its rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tazilite syllogism
Read the passage and outline the three premises: robber enters Fire, everyone in Fire is disgraced, believer is not disgraced. See how they conclude the robber is not a believer.
Notice the verses used: 2:217, 3:192, 66:8.
2
Understand the refutation
The answer denies the general rule (al-kubra) that everyone in Fire is disgraced. Find which verse is limited to the Companions.
3
Reflect on the principle
Consider why this refutation works: a general statement can be restricted by a specific context. This is a common method in kalam.
The answer does not deny the robber enters Fire, only that disgrace applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع - قاطع الطريق يخزى ، لأنه يدخل النار لقوله تعالى : ( ولهم في الآخرة عذاب النار (۱) وكل من يدخل النار يخزى لقوله تعالى حكاية : ربنا إنك من تدخل النار فقد أخزيته) (٢) والمؤمن لا يخزى لقوله تعالى : ( يوم لا يخزي الله النبي والذين آمنوا معه (۳)  وأجيب بمنع الكبرى، فإن الذين آمنوا معه هم الصحابة .
The fourth: The highway robber is disgraced, because he enters the Fire due to His statement: 'And for them in the Hereafter is the punishment of the Fire' (1), and everyone who enters the Fire is disgraced due to His statement quoting: 'Our Lord, indeed whoever You admit to the Fire, You have disgraced him' (2), and the believer is not disgraced due to His statement: 'The Day when Allah will not disgrace the Prophet and those who believed with him' (3). And it was answered by denying the major premise, for those who believed with him are the Companions.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
The Mu'tazila argue as follows: A highway robber is disgraced because he enters Hellfire. Everyone who enters Hell is disgraced (as per Quran 3:192). But a true believer is not disgraced (Quran 66:8). Therefore, the robber cannot be a believer. This would mean that his sin (highway robbery) removes him from iman, so sin is incompatible with iman. The answer is to deny the major premise (man' al-kubra). The major premise is that everyone who enters the Fire is disgraced. The verse about disgrace (3:192) is general, but the verse about believers not being disgraced (66:8) specifically refers to those who believed with the Prophet, i.e., the Companions. It does not apply to all believers, especially sinners. So the robber might be a believer who is punished but not disgraced in the ultimate sense, or the disgrace is specific to the Companions.

Key Terms
خزي
كبرى
صحابة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Everyone who enters Hell is perpetually disgraced.
Correction: The Quranic verse about disgrace (3:192) is general, but the verse about believers not being disgraced (66:8) is specific to the Companions, so not all who enter Hell are disgraced.

Checkpoint
What is the major premise (al-kubra) that the answer denies in the fourth proof?
A) That the robber enters the Fire
B) That everyone who enters the Fire is disgraced
C) That the believer is not disgraced
D) That the robber is a sinner

Key Takeaway
The refutation of the fourth proof shows that a general Quranic verse can be restricted by a specific one, so not all sinners in Hell are disgraced in the ultimate sense.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you live as though your sins will ultimately disgrace you before Allah, or do you trust in His promise not to disgrace those who believe? What specific sin are you holding onto because you think it's too big for His mercy?
?
The refutation shows that a general threatening verse can be restricted by a specific promise. When you read verses about punishment, do you automatically apply them to yourself, or do you recall the specific promises of mercy for believers? How does that affect your repentance?
?
If you were in the position of the highway robber (a sinful believer), would you despair of Allah's mercy or hope in His promise not to disgrace believers? Which mindset dominates your daily relationship with Allah?

The Fifth Proof: The Hadith on Adultery and the Answer of Taghliz
Mu'tazila citation and Ash'ari refutation via taghliz

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili argument from the hadith 'لا يزني الزاني وهو مؤمن' and the Ash'ari refutation that it is a severe warning (taghliz) rather than a literal negation of iman.

Core Idea
Prophetic warnings can be hyperbolic; they do not strip the believer of faith.

The Mu'tazila present a hadith that appears to say a believer cannot commit adultery or theft. They use this to argue that major sins negate iman. The Ash'ari response is remarkably concise: it is a severe warning (taghliz). This lesson unpacks that one-word answer and its significance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Mu'tazili claim
Read the hadith carefully and understand how the Mu'tazila interpret it literally to mean that iman is absent during sin.
2
Understand the Ash'ari answer
The response is 'taghliz' (severe warning). Reflect on what this term implies about the nature of the hadith.
Taghliz means intensification, not literal negation.
3
Apply the concept
Think of other examples in religious texts where hyperbolic language is used to strongly discourage an action without meaning a literal loss of faith.
This helps internalize the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس - قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا يزني الزاني وهو مؤمن، ولا يسرق السارق وهـو مؤمن» (٤) قلنا : تغليظ .
The fifth: His saying, peace be upon him: 'The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer, and the thief does not steal while he is a believer' (4). We said: [It is] a severe warning (taghliz).
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
The Mu'tazila present a well-known hadith: an adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer, and a thief does not steal while he is a believer. This is taken to mean that iman is absent during the act of sin, so sin negates iman. The answer is one word: 'taghliz' (تغليظ), meaning a severe warning or exaggeration. The hadith is meant to deter by emphasizing the enormity of the sin, not that iman is literally removed. The believer still has iman in essence, but the warning is intensified.

Key Terms
تغليظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith is taken literally to mean that a person committing a major sin has no iman at all during the act.
Correction: The hadith is a severe warning (taghliz), meant to deter by exaggeration, not to state a literal fact. The believer retains iman even while sinning, though the sin is grave.

Checkpoint
How do the Mu'tazila interpret the hadith 'لا يزني الزاني وهو مؤمن'?
A) As a literal statement that the sinner ceases to be a believer
B) As a metaphorical description of sin
C) As a command to avoid sin
D) As a proof that iman is only in the heart

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari school interprets the hadith as a severe warning (taghliz) rather than a literal negation of iman.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you commit a sin, do you ever feel your iman is completely gone? How does the concept of taghliz change your understanding of your own faith during moments of weakness?
?

?

The Sixth Proof: Actions as Indicators of Disbelief
Mu'tazila proof and Sunni response on actions as signs of disbelief

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Ahl al-Sunna respond to the Mu'tazila argument that actions can be disbelief by distinguishing between the essence of disbelief and its indicators.

Core Idea
Actions can be signs of disbelief without being disbelief itself.

The Mu'tazila argue that if iman were only inner attestation, then no external action could be considered disbelief. But actions like prostrating to an idol are clearly kufr. Therefore, iman must include the performance of good deeds and avoidance of bad ones. In this passage, the response clarifies that such actions are not disbelief in themselves but are signs that point to underlying denial.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Mu'tazila argument
Read the first part of the passage: 'If it were mere attestation, then nothing of actions and statements would constitute disbelief.' Recognize that the Mu'tazila are building a logical proof: if iman is only inner, then no outer act could be kufr. But they observe that some acts are considered kufr, so iman must include the outward dimension.
The term 'mere attestation' (مجرد التصديق) is key—it refers to inner belief alone.
2
Examine the Sunni response
Now read the answer: 'It is permissible for the Lawgiver to make some sins an indication of denial, like prostrating to an idol.' Notice that the response does not deny that certain actions are associated with disbelief. Instead, it reclassifies them as signs (إمارة) of the inner state of denial (تكذيب). The action itself is not disbelief; it is a strong indicator that reveals or confirms the inner denial.
This distinction is crucial: actions are not the essence of disbelief but can be evidence for it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس - لو كان مجرد التصديق لما كفر بشيء من الأفعال والأقوال . قلنا : يجوز أن يجعل الشارع بعض المعاصي إمارة التكذيب كسجدة الصنم .
The sixth: If it were mere attestation, then nothing of actions and statements would constitute disbelief. We said: It is permissible for the Lawgiver to make some sins an indication of denial, like prostrating to an idol.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
The Mu'tazila argue that if iman is only attestation in the heart, then actions like prostrating to an idol or speaking words of disbelief would not be kufr. But they are kufr, so iman must include the opposite actions (i.e., avoiding such acts). The answer is that the Lawgiver (al-shari') can make certain sins 'imārah al-takdhīb' (إمارة التكذيب) – signs or indicators of actual denial. For example, prostrating to an idol is a strong indicator that the person has rejected Allah in their heart, but the action itself is not literally kufr; it points to the inner denial. So actions can be signs of disbelief without being the essence of disbelief.

Key Terms
إمارة
تكذيب
سجدة الصنم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: An action like prostration to an idol is itself disbelief (kufr).
Correction: It is an indicator (imāra) of underlying denial, not disbelief itself. The action points to inner denial but is not the essence of disbelief.

Checkpoint
What is the Mu'tazila's sixth proof that iman must include actions?
A) Actions are rewarded or punished, so they must be part of iman
B) If iman were mere attestation, then no action would be kufr, but some actions are kufr
C) The Quran commands actions, so they are part of iman
D) The Prophet said that actions are part of iman

Key Takeaway
Actions like prostration to an idol are not disbelief in themselves but are signs that the Lawgiver has made indicators of inner denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone's iman based on an outward action, forgetting that actions are only indicators? How will you change your judgment after learning this lesson?
?
Think of a sin you committed that made you feel you had lost your faith. How does the distinction between the sin itself and it being an indicator of denial affect your understanding of your own relationship with Allah?
?
If prostration to an idol is only an indicator, not the reality of disbelief, what does that say about the state of the heart? How urgently should you guard your heart against hidden denial?

The Seventh Proof: Attestation and Disbelief Distinguished
Mu'tazila argue attestation exists without legal iman; answer distinguishes types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila's claim that attestation coexists with disbelief does not disprove the necessity of heartfelt attestation for true faith.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila confuse incomplete or verbal attestation with genuine heartfelt belief.

In this passage, the Mu'tazila present their seventh proof against the idea that iman is simply attestation. They point to polytheists and hypocrites who have some form of belief yet are not considered believers. The answer reveals the key distinction: not all 'believing' is equal. We'll see how the commentators refute this by showing that these examples lack complete or sincere attestation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the Mu'tazila's argument and the response.
Notice how the Mu'tazila use Quranic verses as evidence.
2
Identify the two groups cited
The Mu'tazila cite polytheists who believe in Allah but associate partners, and hypocrites who profess belief verbally.
These are from Quran 12:106 and 2:8 (or similar).
3
Understand the refutation
The answer distinguishes: the first group's attestation is only in Allah alone (incomplete due to shirk); the second group's is only by the tongue (not heartfelt).
Thus, neither has genuine, complete attestation.
4
Reflect on the implication
This shows that true faith requires sincere, comprehensive attestation of the heart.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابع - قد يثبت التصديق مع نفي الإيمان الشرعي وما يؤمن أكثرهم بالله إلا وهم مشركون (٥) ومن الناس من يقول آمنا بالله . . ) (٦) الآية . قلنا : لأن الأول تصديق بالله وحده والثاني باللسان فقط.
The seventh: Attestation may be established along with the negation of legal iman, as in 'And most of them believe not in Allah except while they associate others with Him' (5) and 'And of the people are those who say, 'We believe in Allah...' (6) the verse. We said: Because the first is attestation in Allah alone and the second is only by the tongue.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
The Mu'tazila point out that there are people who have some form of attestation (tasdiq) yet are not considered believers in the legal sense. They cite two Quranic examples: (1) the polytheists who believe in Allah but associate partners (Quran 12:106), and (2) the hypocrites who say with their tongues that they believe (Quran 2:8). They argue that if attestation alone were enough, these people would be believers, but they are not, so legal iman must require actions. The answer distinguishes: the first group's attestation is 'tasdiq billahi wahdahu' (attestation in Allah alone) but they also associate partners, so their attestation is incomplete; the second group's attestation is only verbal, not heartfelt. Thus, they lack genuine attestation, so the argument fails.

Key Terms
إيمان شرعي
تصديق
لسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the polytheists and hypocrites have true attestation (tasdiq) and thus demonstrate that attestation does not equal iman.
Correction: The polytheists have incomplete attestation (only tawhid without rejecting shirk), and the hypocrites have only verbal attestation without heartfelt conviction. Therefore, they lack genuine, complete tasdiq.

Checkpoint
Which two groups are cited by the Mu'tazila to show that attestation can exist without legal iman?
A) The Jews and Christians
B) The polytheists who believe in Allah but associate partners, and the hypocrites who say they believe
C) The atheists and agnostics
D) The sinners and the neglectful

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila's examples of polytheists and hypocrites do not disprove that iman requires genuine heartfelt attestation, as their attestation is either incomplete or merely verbal.

The Eighth Proof: Iman and Sin Cannot Coexist?
Mu'tazili argument and refutation on iman and sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Mu'tazili argument that iman and sin are incompatible, and how the refutation distinguishes between aspects of praise and blame.

Core Idea
A sinner can deserve both praise and blame from different aspects.

This lesson presents the eighth Mu'tazili argument that iman and major sin cannot coexist because they entail contradictory judgments of praise and blame. It then provides the refutation, which resolves the apparent contradiction by recognizing that a person can be praiseworthy for their faith and blameworthy for their sin from different perspectives.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: the Mu'tazila claim, their Quranic evidence, the contradiction they assert, and the response that follows.
The response begins with 'قلنا' (we said).
2
Identify the key terms
Understand the terms مدح (praise), ذم (blame), عاصي (sinner), and كامل الإيمان (complete faith) as used in the argument.
3
Understand the refutation strategy
The response says the sinner deserves both praise and blame 'min wajh' (from one aspect) — meaning each from a different aspect. This resolves the contradiction.
The ultimate, utmost praise is reserved for the one with complete iman, free from sin.
4
Connect to the broader issue
The refutation leads to the claim that actions are not part of the reality of iman, which will be elaborated in subsequent pages.
This is a key point in the debate about the definition of iman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثامن - الإيمان ينبيء عن استحقاق غاية المدح على ما يشعر به قوله تعالى: إنه من عبادنا المؤمنين (۷) فينافي استحقاق الذم الكبير . قلنا : العاصي يستحق كلاً من وجه ، وإنما غاية المدح لكامل الإيمان) الأعمال غير داخلة في حقيقة الإيمان لوجوه :
The eighth: Iman indicates entitlement to utmost praise, as indicated by His statement: 'Indeed, he was of Our believing servants' (7), conflicting with entitlement to great blame. We said: The sinner deserves each from one aspect, and utmost praise is for complete iman) Actions are not included in the reality of iman for reasons:
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
The Mu'tazila argue that the Quran describes believers as deserving utmost praise (e.g., 'he was of Our believing servants' in several verses of Surah al-Saffat). If a believer commits a major sin, they would deserve both praise and blame, but praise and blame are contradictory. Therefore, a sinner cannot have complete iman, so sin must negate iman. The answer states that a sinner (al-asi) deserves both praise and blame 'min wajh' (from one aspect), i.e., from different perspectives. The ultimate, utmost praise is for 'kamil al-iman' (complete iman), which is free from sin. So the objection does not prove that actions are part of the reality of iman. The passage then concludes with a statement: 'Actions are not included in the reality of iman for reasons:' (الأعمال غير داخلة في حقيقة الإيمان لوجوه), which is the author's positive claim that will be elaborated in the following pages.

Key Terms
مدح
ذم
عاصي
كامل الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A sinning believer cannot deserve any praise at all.
Correction: They still deserve praise for their iman, though the ultimate, highest praise is for the sinless.

Checkpoint
How does the refutation resolve the contradiction between praise and blame for a sinning believer?
A) By denying that a sinning believer has any iman
B) By stating that the sinner deserves both praise and blame from different aspects
C) By arguing that the Quranic verse is not applicable
D) By claiming that major sin is not blameworthy

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazili proof is refuted by showing that a sinner can simultaneously deserve praise for iman and blame for sin, as they are from different aspects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Recall a sin you committed that made you feel as if your faith was completely tarnished. According to this lesson, do you still deserve praise for your iman? Honestly, do you think you still have iman despite that sin? How does that realization impact your view of yourself and your relationship with Allah? Will you let it lead you to complacency or to deeper gratitude and repentance?
?
The Mu'tazila argued that praise and blame cannot coexist in one person. When you sin, do you feel like your good deeds are erased? This lesson says a sinner still deserves praise for iman. Does that comfort you or make you less concerned about sin? What does this teach about the balance between hope and fear? Commit to one concrete action today to strengthen your iman while acknowledging your shortcomings.
?
How often do you judge other Muslims who commit sins, assuming they have little or no faith? This lesson teaches that a sinner can still have iman and deserve praise for it. Will you change how you view and treat fellow believers who struggle with sin? What specific step will you take to see them through the lens of this teaching?

The Linguistic and Eschatological Proofs
Sanusi presents the first two proofs that actions are not part of iman.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first two proofs that actions are not part of faith: the linguistic argument that faith means assent, and the eschatological argument that only assent benefits at death.

Core Idea
At death, only assent and speech matter; actions have no room.

The author begins with two foundational proofs. The first is linguistic: the word 'iman' means assent, with no evidence it was transferred to include actions. The second is eschatological: at the moment of death, only assent and verbal acknowledgment are beneficial, as actions are no longer possible. These set the stage for further scriptural arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for both proofs
Read the Arabic and translation, noting how each proof is introduced with 'الأول' and 'الثاني'.
Focus on the logical structure: 'what has passed' refers to earlier discussion on the meaning of iman.
2
Understand the first proof
Iman is defined as tasdiq (assent). There is no evidence (naql) that the term's meaning was transferred to include actions.
This is a linguistic argument: the original meaning is narrow.
3
Understand the second proof
Text and consensus show that faith does not benefit at the sight of punishment and is called despair. Only tasdiq and iqrar are relevant because there is no room for actions at death.
This proof uses both revelation and rational observation.
4
Reflect on the connection
Consider how these two proofs complement each other: one from definition, one from practical consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأعمال غير داخلة في حقيقة الإيمان لوجوه : الأول - ما مر أنه اسم للتصديق، ولا دليل على النقل. الثاني - النص والإجماع على أنه لا ينفع عند معاينة العذاب، ويسمى اليأس، ولا خفاء في أن ذلك إنما هو التصديق والإقرار، إذ لا مجال للأعمال. الثالث - النصوص الدالة على الأوامر والنواهي بعد إثبات الإيمان كقوله تعالى: (يا أيها الذين آمنوا كتب عليكم الصيام) (۱) الرابع - النصوص الدالة على أن الإيمان والأعمال أمران متفارقان، كقوله تعالى : إن الذين آمنوا وعملوا الصالحات (۲) ومن يؤمن بالله ويعمل صالحاً (۳) ومن يأته مؤمناً قد عمل الصالحات(٤) ومن يعمل من الصالحات وهو مؤمن (٥) وسئل النبي [؟] عن أفضل الأعمال فقال : إيمان لا شك فيه، وجهاد لا غلول فيه، وحج مبرور (1) . الخامس - الآيات الدالة على أن الإيمان والمعاصي قد يجتمعان، كقوله تعالى: (الذين آمنوا ولم يلبسوا إيمانهم بظلم (۷) والذين آمنوا ولم يهاجروا (۸) وإن طائفتان من المؤمنين اقتتلوا . . (۹) الآية كما أخرجك ربك من بيتك بالحق وإن فريقاً من المؤمنين لكارهون (۱۰)
Actions are not included in the reality of faith (ḥaqīqat al-īmān) for [several] aspects: First: What has passed that it [faith] is a name for assent (taṣdīq), and there is no evidence for transference (naql) [of the meaning]. Second: The text (naṣṣ) and consensus (ijmāʿ) that it [faith] does not benefit at the sight of punishment, and is called despair; and it is not hidden that that is only assent and acknowledgment (iqrār), for there is no room for actions. Third: The texts indicating commands and prohibitions after the affirmation of faith, like His saying: 'O you who have believed, decreed upon you is fasting.' Fourth: The texts indicating that faith and actions are two separate matters, like His saying: 'Indeed those who believe and do righteous deeds' and 'Whoever believes in Allah and does righteousness' and 'Whoever comes to Him as a believer having done righteous deeds' and 'Whoever does righteous deeds while he is a believer.' And the Prophet [?] was asked about the best deeds, so he said: 'Faith without doubt, jihad without cheating, and an accepted pilgrimage.' Fifth: The verses indicating that faith and sins may coincide, like His saying: 'Those who believe and do not confuse their faith with wrongdoing' and 'Those who believe and have not emigrated' and 'If two parties among the believers fight' the verse, and 'As your Lord brought you out of your house with truth while indeed a party of the believers were unwilling.'
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage lists five proofs (wujūh) that actions (aʿmāl) are not part of the reality of faith (ḥaqīqat al-īmān). Each proof is drawn from textual and rational sources. First proof: Faith is linguistically assent (taṣdīq); there is no evidence (naql) that the term's meaning has been transferred to include actions. Second proof: At the moment of death (muʿāyanat al-ʿadhāb), only assent and verbal acknowledgment (iqrār) are beneficial, not actions, as the sources state that faith at that point is called despair (yaʾs) and is not accepted. Third proof: The Qurʾān addresses believers with commands (e.g., fasting) after affirming their faith, showing that faith is prior and distinct from actions. Fourth proof: Many Qurʾānic verses juxtapose 'īmān' and 'ʿamal ṣāliḥ' as two separate categories (e.g., 'those who believe and do righteous deeds'), and a hadith lists faith as the best deed whereas actions like jihad and pilgrimage are separate. Fifth proof: Qurʾānic verses affirm that believers can commit sins (e.g., fighting among themselves, reluctance in battle) without losing their identity as believers, proving that faith and sin coexist.

Key Terms
تصديق
نقل
إقرار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second proof, what is the term for faith when it is seen at death?
A) Taṣdīq
B) Yaʾs (despair)
C) ʿAmal
D) Ijmāʿ

Key Takeaway
The first two proofs establish that iman is fundamentally assent, not action, and that at death only assent matters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If at the moment of death only your inner assent and verbal declaration matter—and your actions are of no avail—then what is the state of your heart right now? Are you truly convinced of the truth of Islam, or are you relying on your deeds to make up for a lack of certainty?
?
Knowing that actions are not part of the reality of iman, how much of your spiritual energy is spent on polishing your outward performance while neglecting the core of your faith? Will you commit today to examining your inner conviction before your next action?
?
The second proof shows that faith at the sight of punishment is rejected. If you were to stand before Allah at this moment, would your iman be accepted? What prevents you from turning to Him now with pure assent and acknowledgment, without delay?

Scriptural Commands and the Pairing of Faith and Works
Sanusi provides proofs 3 and 4: commands after faith and separate mention of faith and works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quranic commands and the pairing of faith with works show that faith and actions are distinct.

Core Idea
The Quran addresses believers with commands, proving faith precedes action.

The third and fourth proofs use direct Quranic evidence. The third proof cites verses where Allah addresses the believers with commands (like fasting), indicating that faith is already present before action. The fourth proof lists many Quranic verses that pair 'iman' and 'amal salih' as two separate things, and a hadith that distinguishes faith from jihad and hajj. These show they are not identical.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage for proofs 3 and 4
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the Quranic examples and the hadith.
The third proof is concise; the fourth proof is more detailed.
2
Understand the third proof
Allah says 'O you who have believed, decreed upon you is fasting.' The command to fast comes after affirming faith, showing faith is a prerequisite, not something established by the action.
The verse is from Surah Al-Baqarah 2:183.
3
Understand the fourth proof
Multiple Quranic verses say 'those who believe and do righteous deeds', treating faith and deeds as separate. The Prophet also listed faith as a distinct 'best deed' compared to jihad and hajj.
This linguistic pairing indicates two different realities.
4
Reflect on the implication
If actions were part of faith, the Quran would not need to mention them separately after mentioning faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Second: The text (naṣṣ) and consensus (ijmāʿ) that it [faith] does not benefit at the sight of punishment, and is called despair; and it is not hidden that that is only assent and acknowledgment (iqrār), for there is no room for actions. Fourth: The texts indicating that faith and actions are two separate matters, like His saying: 'Indeed those who believe and do righteous deeds' and 'Whoever believes in Allah and does righteousness' and 'Whoever comes to Him as a believer having done righteous deeds' and 'Whoever does righteous deeds while he is a believer.' Commentary
This passage lists five proofs (wujūh) that actions (aʿmāl) are not part of the reality of faith (ḥaqīqat al-īmān). Each proof is drawn from textual and rational sources. First proof: Faith is linguistically assent (taṣdīq); there is no evidence (naql) that the term's meaning has been transferred to include actions. Fourth proof: Many Qurʾānic verses juxtapose 'īmān' and 'ʿamal ṣāliḥ' as two separate categories (e.g., 'those who believe and do righteous deeds'), and a hadith lists faith as the best deed whereas actions like jihad and pilgrimage are separate. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some believe that because faith and righteous deeds are often mentioned together, they are one and the same.
Correction: The author argues that the very act of mentioning them separately shows they are two distinct things, not that they are inseparable in definition.

Checkpoint
What is the key evidence in the fourth proof that faith and actions are separate?
A) A single verse that defines faith as action
B) The use of the word 'and' between faith and actions in many verses
C) A consensus of scholars
D) The command to fast

Key Takeaway
Commands like fasting are given to believers, and the Quran consistently separates 'iman' from 'amal' using 'and', proving they are distinct.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a command from Allah (like prayer or fasting), do you first examine whether your heart has true faith, or do you rush to perform the action mechanically? What would change if you prioritized faith before every deed?
?
The hadith lists faith without doubt as the best deed, ahead of jihad and pilgrimage. Which of these three is most missing in your life right now? What is one step you can take today to strengthen your faith over your actions?
?
If faith and deeds are distinct, then even the most righteous deeds cannot compensate for a weak faith. Does this truth make you feel more dependent on Allah's mercy or more anxious? How can you turn that feeling into sincere reliance on Him?
